        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2829697252" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5299075132913836592">This turned out to be an absolutely ideal audiobook to listen to as I walked my dog each morning. Admittedly I was walking in the suburbs of Sydney and Lillian was in the middle of New York but we were both walking and it seemed apt. It also meant I read the book a little each day which worked well for me.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29939353.Lillian_Boxfish_Takes_a_Walk' title='Lillian Boxfish Takes a Walk by Kathleen Rooney' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lillian Boxfish Takes a Walk</a> is a slow burn of a story, beautifully written and worth absorbing properly. It is based on the life of a real person and all the events and the settings rang true.</span>
  <span id="freeText5299075132913836592" style="display:none">This turned out to be an absolutely ideal audiobook to listen to as I walked my dog each morning. Admittedly I was walking in the suburbs of Sydney and Lillian was in the middle of New York but we were both walking and it seemed apt. It also meant I read the book a little each day which worked well for me.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29939353.Lillian_Boxfish_Takes_a_Walk" title="Lillian Boxfish Takes a Walk by Kathleen Rooney" rel="nofollow noopener">Lillian Boxfish Takes a Walk</a> is a slow burn of a story, beautifully written and worth absorbing properly. It is based on the life of a real person and all the events and the settings rang true. I must admit to not liking Lillian very much. She was a little too smart, her wit a bit too caustic - a person who would make me feel uncomfortable in real life. However she was admirable in the way she tackled life and the way she coped with some major traumas along the way.<br /><br />The whole book was very nicely put together as it meandered back and forth between Lillian's life story and the current events of New Year's Eve 1984. I enjoyed it very much.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1819439327" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1819439327" />
    <a title="DeB MaRtEnS" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9827967-deb-martens"><img alt="DeB MaRtEnS" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593294620p2/9827967.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1819439327?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="DeB MaRtEnS" class="user" itemprop="url" name="DeB MaRtEnS" href="/user/show/9827967-deb-martens">DeB MaRtEnS</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1819439327" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18379055362981502191">"...I got my idea to combine my love of (Margaret) Fishback with my love of cities and flaniêre; I resolved to write a novel that would bring these two affinities together." Kathleen Rooney, author of Lillian Boxfish Takes a Walk. <br/><br/>And so, we are introduced to Lillian, a fictional representative of the once esteemed and highly paid advertising copy writer for R.H. Macy, New York for two decades beginning in the 1930s. Like Dorothy Parker who followed Fishback, snappy wit gave her recognition, as </span>
  <span id="freeText18379055362981502191" style="display:none">"...I got my idea to combine my love of (Margaret) Fishback with my love of cities and flaniêre; I resolved to write a novel that would bring these two affinities together." Kathleen Rooney, author of Lillian Boxfish Takes a Walk. <br /><br />And so, we are introduced to Lillian, a fictional representative of the once esteemed and highly paid advertising copy writer for R.H. Macy, New York for two decades beginning in the 1930s. Like Dorothy Parker who followed Fishback, snappy wit gave her recognition, as well as her poetry which was gently irreverent about marriage. <br /><br />The novel follows Lillian's "flaniêre" or promenade through the old city of New York, on New Year's Eve in 1985. The city is showing wear, crime an issue at this point in time and its citizens have gradually moved out to the suburbs. Lillian is 85, a New York devotee and determined to remain in the place which identifies her and is her home. She doing her best to be fashionably dressed and maintain her long daily walks, but she is conscious that she too is showing wear and that her once large social circle has dwindled from death or departure, leaving her isolated. <br /><br />As she walks, she notes the architectural landmarks of her life, and with them, the significant events which shaped her. Kathleen Rooney is eloquent with the language of Lillian's inner self, drifting from the lyrically poetic to the caustically precise, creating an intensely dynamic character. <br /><br />I loved Lillian as she entered mid-life, developing empathy, maturity even though it was caused by deep personal pain. THAT Lillian suddenly had context to the elderly woman, wise and contemplative on her grand promenade. <br /><br />"...it's still not comprehensible that such an estrangement of affection could cause a person to completely break down. Make them unable to pack a suitcase...". Dealing with the complete collapse of her marriage, her adored husband's involvement with his secretary, Lillian falls apart and spends time in a facility healing. After the divorce, Lillian's son lives with her and she continues to work as a freelancer. <br /><br />As Lillian walked, I was touched by her efforts to interact with the community which she was on the point of losing altogether. In a way, I recognized her actions; dealing with a chronic illness myself, work colleagues and active friendships fall away leaving one with an altered sense of identity. A chat with the waitstaff, the barman, the limo driver, the pregnant lady, the corner store vendor - gave Lillian a bit of a chance to recall the substance of actively "being". Lillian wasn't about to give up. She would make her life her own, whatever came. <br /><br />Four stars, because I loved the last half of the book and because the writing is exquisite.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18379055362981502191" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12422935137035303448">This is somewhere between a 3.5 - 4 stars for me, but I'll round up because that ending was fantastic. I could tell the author was also a poet for most of the novel, but the way she was able to succinctly and powerfully tie up the whole thing was definitely poetic. Lillian Boxfish is a great character, based on the real-life Margaret Fishback. I loved the historical aspect of this, especially as the book takes place on the last evening of 1984 while Lillian takes a walk around NYC and remembers </span>
  <span id="freeText12422935137035303448" style="display:none">This is somewhere between a 3.5 - 4 stars for me, but I'll round up because that ending was fantastic. I could tell the author was also a poet for most of the novel, but the way she was able to succinctly and powerfully tie up the whole thing was definitely poetic. Lillian Boxfish is a great character, based on the real-life Margaret Fishback. I loved the historical aspect of this, especially as the book takes place on the last evening of 1984 while Lillian takes a walk around NYC and remembers the last 80 years of her life. It had a sort of nostalgia to it, but the kind that you recognize as its happening and vow to hold on to in the future. I really enjoyed it and would recommend to anyone who is looking for a touching, funny, and sweet read.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2193232907?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess | thegreeneyedreader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess | thegreeneyedreader" href="/user/show/43561053-jess-thegreeneyedreader">Jess | thegreeneyedreader</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/31204493-lillian-boxfish-takes-a-walk">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2193232907" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2478287662714317886">I enjoyed Lillian so much. I loved her. <div id="review_1961769629" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1961769629" />
    <a title="Bianca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29843800-bianca"><img alt="Bianca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589154116p2/29843800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1961769629?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bianca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bianca" href="/user/show/29843800-bianca">Bianca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781427282385" href="/book/show/34033691-lillian-boxfish-takes-a-walk">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29843800-bianca?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29843800-bianca?shelf=middle-age-characters-or-older">middle-age-characters-or-older</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29843800-bianca?shelf=us-author">us-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29843800-bianca?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29843800-bianca?shelf=debut-novel">debut-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29843800-bianca?shelf=female-author">female-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29843800-bianca?shelf=first-person-narrator">first-person-narrator</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1961769629" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10833278456995350373">It's the last day of 1984 and the octogenarian Lillian Boxfish is walking around New York, as she'd done for six decades. You see, Lillian is a walker. Walking has saved her life.<br/><br/>While going from place to place, Lillian retraces many of her life's milestones: moving to New York, in search of adventure and to escape her parents; her much loved job at Macy's, writing copy; her marriage and motherhood; her subsequent divorce; losing her job because of impending motherhood, and a major nervous break</span>
  <span id="freeText10833278456995350373" style="display:none">It's the last day of 1984 and the octogenarian Lillian Boxfish is walking around New York, as she'd done for six decades. You see, Lillian is a walker. Walking has saved her life.<br /><br />While going from place to place, Lillian retraces many of her life's milestones: moving to New York, in search of adventure and to escape her parents; her much loved job at Macy's, writing copy; her marriage and motherhood; her subsequent divorce; losing her job because of impending motherhood, and a major nervous breakdown.<br /><br />It's impossible not to love Lillian Boxfish, who was vivacious, loquacious, intelligent, creative and hard-working. She was ahead of her time and didn't care for conventions, while still fitting in and making a successful living as the highest paid female in advertising.<br /><br />Because it was told in the first person, this novel had the feel of an autobiography. At times it got a bit dull, but then, life can be dull, and it seems to get more and more so as we age. What can one do? <i>"The point of living in the world is just to stay interested."</i> If only it were that easy. One can be interested in the world, but it's painful as hell when the world is no longer interested in us. I wonder if men feel this as acutely as women do? <br /><br />While I liked this novel a lot, I would have liked to get to know more intimately some of the people who played an important role in Lillian's life. Even when it came to her relationship with her husband, Max, I never quite felt the love, although Lillian told us how much she loved him and that he was the love of her life. <br /><br />Nevertheless, despite some minor quibbles, I thoroughly enjoyed traveling alongside Lillian. If anything, it was a great reminder to walk more often.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10833278456995350373" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2098463338" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2098463338" />
    <a title="Chrissie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/632247-chrissie"><img alt="Chrissie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1321799585p2/632247.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2098463338?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chrissie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chrissie" href="/user/show/632247-chrissie">Chrissie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=hf">hf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=audible-uk">audible-uk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=bio">bio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=returned">returned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=2017-read">2017-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=nyc">nyc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=usa">usa</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2098463338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3617094214154735142">ETA: In my view, the narrator of the audiobook does not distort the author's message but intensifies it, and the message itself I dislike.<br/><br/>******************<br/><br/>This novel is inspired by the life of Margaret Fishback. Haven't heard of her? Neither had I! Here is a quick resumé: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Margaret_Fishback'>https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Margare...</a><br/>Go ahead and read it. It is not going to wreck the story. What is presented are merely the bones on which the fictional story is drawn. Fishback died in 1985. When Lillian dies, we do no</span>
  <span id="freeText3617094214154735142" style="display:none">ETA: In my view, the narrator of the audiobook does not distort the author's message but intensifies it, and the message itself I dislike.<br /><br />******************<br /><br />This novel is inspired by the life of Margaret Fishback. Haven't heard of her? Neither had I! Here is a quick resumé: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Margaret_Fishback">https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Margare...</a><br />Go ahead and read it. It is not going to wreck the story. What is presented are merely the bones on which the fictional story is drawn. Fishback died in 1985. When Lillian dies, we do not know. <br /><br />This is a book about Lillian Boxfish. NYC is her home and had been so since the 30s. It is the last day of 1984. It's New Year's Eve. She is 85 and she is to take a walk. This is not strange; NYC is <b>her home</b> and these are <b>her</b> streets and <b>walking is what she does</b>, besides being that woman at Macy's who had been “the highest-paid advertising woman in the world.” What <b>is</b> different is that we are with her on her walk and we are with her as she looks back on her life. On this night, the mood in the city is anxious. There is at large in the streets of Manhattan a subway vigilante, but when hasn’t a walk at night in Manhattan ever been without danger?! <br /><br />I listened to the audiobook narrated by Xe Sands. I have an extremely hard time separating the author's words from the tone with which the story was read. Sands voice quavers and trembles. This is not merely the quavering that comes with old age. I heard regret and sorrow and misgiving. Does Sands' intonation reflect the message the author wished to convey? <br /><br />If Sands intonation is a correct interpretation of the author’s lines, this is a very sad story. I have a hard time accepting this. And I hope the author is not inferring that how Lillian saw her life mirrors how Margaret Fishback saw her life. I don’t think the author has enough to go on to makes such a claim, so I am just going to see this as a very sad fictional story. <br /><br />New York’s vibrancy scarcely comes through. I am notching up another minus point for this. <br /><br />Lillian’s life made me sad. I do not think her strength made her happy. She is a strong woman, but so very alone. <br /><br />Two stars for the book and two stars for the narration.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3617094214154735142" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3278589334" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">

<div id="review_2850874465" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2850874465" />
    <a title="Richard Derus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3920693-richard-derus"><img alt="Richard Derus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494992210p2/3920693.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2850874465?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard Derus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard Derus" href="/user/show/3920693-richard-derus">Richard Derus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3920693-richard-derus?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2850874465" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2999607631995086911">I have nothing important to add to the conversation about this book except to say that I loved Lillian enough to re-read this book (a thing I consciously avoid doing, too old to waste the eyeblinks when there are literally dozens of new books every week that I want to read). I am living the "ancient Chinese curse" (<a href='https://quoteinvestigator.com/2015/12/18/live/' rel='nofollow noopener'>that's nothing of the sort</a>) often translated as "May you live in interesting times," among other formulations. I was old enough to have my dinner ruined by Vietnam War body counts int</span>
  <span id="freeText2999607631995086911" style="display:none">I have nothing important to add to the conversation about this book except to say that I loved Lillian enough to re-read this book (a thing I consciously avoid doing, too old to waste the eyeblinks when there are literally dozens of new books every week that I want to read). I am living the "ancient Chinese curse" (<a href="https://quoteinvestigator.com/2015/12/18/live/" rel="nofollow noopener">that's nothing of the sort</a>) often translated as "May you live in interesting times," among other formulations. I was old enough to have my dinner ruined by Vietnam War body counts intoned gravely by Uncle Walter on the CBS Evening News. The inner-city uprisings in Newark, Detroit, Oakland, Watts..."Hey Hey LBJ, how many kids did you kill today?"...and now the next skirmish in the unfinished US Civil War as my last full decade on Earth unfolds.<br /><br />I needed Lillian's mentions of The Strand and her gentleman callers and R. H. Macy's and how much she hated admitting when her mother was right. I needed her to walk for me down streets I once loved so immoderately, wearing her deeply unfashionable top-quality mink as a slew of men I loved were dying in St. Vincent's (I was probably in one of their rooms at the time she was walking!), and to feel the full weight of memory. Sometimes it's <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crushing_(execution)#:~:text=Death%20by%20crushing%20or%20pressing,longer%20used%20by%20any%20government." rel="nofollow noopener">death by crushing</a>, sometimes a warm comforter on a cold, windy night.<br /><br />So thank you, Author Rooney. I needed this story to help me see that the only way out is through, to face the storm like Lillian always did, and feel the lovely ache of days gone by but never disappeared.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2999607631995086911" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2026645569" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2026645569" />
    <a title="Stephanie Anze" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27117957-stephanie-anze"><img alt="Stephanie Anze" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604709893p2/27117957.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2026645569?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephanie Anze" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephanie Anze" href="/user/show/27117957-stephanie-anze">Stephanie Anze</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27117957-stephanie-anze?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27117957-stephanie-anze?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2026645569" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6949697060095140792">"What is it with you and walking, Lillian?"<br/><br/>Its the last day of 1984. Lillian boxfish dons orange fire lipstick, riding boots and her mink coat, bids Phoebe (her cat) good bye and walks out of her apartment for her standing appointment at her favorite Italian restaurant. As she sets out on foot, she begins to reminisce about her past. At 85 years young, Lillian has had a interesting life, to say the lest.<br/><br/>Inspired by the real life poet and advertising copywriter, Margaret Fishback, Lillian Boxfish</span>
  <span id="freeText6949697060095140792" style="display:none">"What is it with you and walking, Lillian?"<br /><br />Its the last day of 1984. Lillian boxfish dons orange fire lipstick, riding boots and her mink coat, bids Phoebe (her cat) good bye and walks out of her apartment for her standing appointment at her favorite Italian restaurant. As she sets out on foot, she begins to reminisce about her past. At 85 years young, Lillian has had a interesting life, to say the lest.<br /><br />Inspired by the real life poet and advertising copywriter, Margaret Fishback, Lillian Boxfish is quite a lady. In the apex of her career she was the highest payed ad writer for R. H. Macys and a published poet. Her style is described as wry and jocular, she is considered to have pioneered this style. Outspoken, brass but ultimately with a charming personality, Lillian was both conventional and ahead of the times. While this novel was witty and humorous, there is also a darker undertone to her story. In this regard, this novel reminded me of 'Eleanor Oliphant is Completely Fine'. Both ladies had to overcome rather difficult circumstances, which played a big role in their mannerisms and personalities. Lillian walks through NY city, meets a gamut of people and reflects on her life. At times thoughtful and others witty, this book was an all around enjoyable read. Fortitude. That is Lillian's greatest asset. You will grow to respect this fine lady. Would recommend. A good read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6949697060095140792" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2445456397" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2445456397" />
    <a title="Marina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75392432-marina"><img alt="Marina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518382822p2/75392432.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2445456397?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marina" href="/user/show/75392432-marina">Marina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35290061-lillian-boxfish-takes-a-walk">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2445456397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5971644795063869597">You’ve got a job you love. <br/>You’ve earned respect and success, even though it’s normal to be paid less than a man. <br/>But you’ve met someone. If you marry and have a child (as everyone expects you to), you’ll lose the job you love. <br/>Welcome to twentieth century America, where women are valued for youth and fertility, rather than brains and ability. <br/>It’s enough to drive a girl crazy – or should I say – drive a <i>woman</i> crazy. As Lilian comments - recalling a psychiatrist calling her a ‘reasonable girl’- </span>
  <span id="freeText5971644795063869597" style="display:none">You’ve got a job you love. <br />You’ve earned respect and success, even though it’s normal to be paid less than a man. <br />But you’ve met someone. If you marry and have a child (as everyone expects you to), you’ll lose the job you love. <br />Welcome to twentieth century America, where women are valued for youth and fertility, rather than brains and ability. <br />It’s enough to drive a girl crazy – or should I say – drive a <i>woman</i> crazy. As Lilian comments - recalling a psychiatrist calling her a ‘reasonable girl’- ‘I was not a girl. I was fifty-five.’ <br />In this wonderful book, we walk the streets of 1980s New York with Lilian, now an old woman. But she’s certainly no little old lady, stuck in the past. <br />Despite some occasional quaintness and the odd improbable scene, this is an easy read with real depth.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5971644795063869597" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

		    <b>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Kq7UYZ4PHVyiMZHvR4fEDzscIL1p5sBaO51SF1b6sZe/RjS+mK6KssPfwR7F0kK/mPyyfXsPUI9IrBlh+TV/Cw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('B37i+zeVjkqZsKl8dvXHCoUFKoX1oESEsZPHgmFzMASSlgIkMTQZpPhe+Y30oEG6JuW4RedJ1FHCooz0zrz+mA==')})
  }

Many years later, one sister lives with her black daughter in the same southern town she once tried to escape. The other secretly passes for white, and her white husband knows nothing of her past. Still, even separated by so many miles and just as many lies, the fates of the twins remain intertwined. Looking well beyond issues of race, The Vanishing Half considers the lasting influence of the past as it shapes a person\'s decisions, desires, and expectations, and explores some of the multiple reasons and realms in which people sometimes feel pulled to live as something other than their origins.\n\nAs with her New York Times-bestselling debut The Mothers, Brit Bennett offers an engrossing Jonathan Alkaitis works in finance and owns the hotel. When he passes Vincent his card with a tip, it\'s the beginning of their life together. That same day, Vincent\'s half-brother, Paul, scrawls a note on the windowed wall of the hotel: &quot;Why don\'t you swallow broken glass.&quot; Leon Prevant, a shipping executive for a company called Neptune-Avramidis, sees the note from the hotel bar and is shaken to his core. Thirteen years later Vincent mysteriously disappears from the deck of a Neptune-Avramidis ship. Weaving together the lives of these characters, The Glass Hotel moves between the ship, the skyscrapers of Manhattan, and the wilderness of northern Vancouver Island, painting a breathtaking picture           <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3528.Kathleen_Rooney"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1467996025p3/3528.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3752773462887483950">Kathleen Rooney is a founding editor of Rose Metal Press, a publisher of literary work in hybrid genres, and a founding member of Poems While You Wait, a team of poets and their typewriters who compose commissioned poetry on demand. She teaches English and Creative Writing at DePaul University and is the author of eight books of poetry, nonfiction, and fiction, including the novel O, Democracy! (F</span>
  <span id="freeText3752773462887483950" style="display:none">Kathleen Rooney is a founding editor of Rose Metal Press, a publisher of literary work in hybrid genres, and a founding member of Poems While You Wait, a team of poets and their typewriters who compose commissioned poetry on demand. She teaches English and Creative Writing at DePaul University and is the author of eight books of poetry, nonfiction, and fiction, including the novel O, Democracy! (Fifth Star Press, 2014) and the novel in poems Robinson Alone (Gold Wake Press, 2012). With Eric Plattner, she is the co-editor of René Magritte: Selected Writings (University of Minnesota Press, 2016 and Alma Books, 2016). A winner of a Ruth Lilly Fellowship from Poetry magazine, her reviews and criticism have appeared in the New York Times Book Review, The Chicago Tribune, The New York Times Magazine, The Rumpus, The Nation the Poetry Foundation website and elsewhere. She lives in Chicago with her spouse, the writer Martin Seay, and her second novel, Lillian Boxfish Takes a Walk, will be published by St. Martin’s Press in January of 2017.</span>
